					<h1 id="section_0">Comcast</h1>

				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Comcast Corp.">Comcast Corp.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Comcast Corporation</b> (formerly registered as <b>Comcast Holdings</b>)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[note 1]</a></sup> is an American <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">conglomerate</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> It is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting" title="Broadcasting">broadcasting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable television</a> company in the world by revenue and the largest pay-TV company, the largest cable TV company and largest home <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service provider</a> in the United States, and the nation's third-largest home <a href="/wiki/Telephone_service_provider" class="mw-redirect" title="Telephone service provider">telephone service provider</a>. Comcast services U.S. residential and commercial customers in 40 states and in the <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">District of Columbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-annual_report_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annual_report-10">[9]</a></sup> As the parent company of the international media company <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a> since 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Jan-2011-8-K_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Jan-2011-8-K-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Feb-2013-8-K_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Feb-2013-8-K-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Mar-2013-8-K_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Mar-2013-8-K-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CMCSA-GE_Final_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMCSA-GE_Final-14">[13]</a></sup> Comcast is a producer of <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">feature films</a> and <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> programs intended for theatrical exhibition and over-the-air and cable television broadcast, respectively.

income</a></div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$71.613 billion</span> (2018)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Owner</th><td <li><a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sky_Group" title="Sky Group">Sky Group</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Comcast_Spectacor" title="Comcast Spectacor">Comcast Spectacor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leisure_Arts" title="Leisure Arts">Leisure Arts</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Midco" title="Midco">Midco</a> (49%)</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://corporate.comcast.com">corporate<wbr></wbr>.comcast<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-CNN_Money_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Money-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_Markets_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_Markets-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mediadb.eu_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mediadb.eu-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10-K_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K-7">[7]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Comcast owns and operates the <a href="/wiki/Xfinity" title="Xfinity">Xfinity</a> residential cable communications subsidiary, Comcast Business, a commercial services provider, Xfinity Mobile, an <a href="/wiki/MVNO" class="mw-redirect" title="MVNO">MVNO</a> of <a href="/wiki/Verizon" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon">Verizon</a>, over-the-air national broadcast network channels (<a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">Telemundo</a>, <a href="/wiki/TeleXitos" title="TeleXitos">TeleXitos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cozi_TV" title="Cozi TV">Cozi TV</a>), multiple cable-only channels (including <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/USA_Network" title="USA Network">USA Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syfy" title="Syfy">Syfy</a>, <a href="/wiki/NBCSN" title="NBCSN">NBCSN</a>, and <a href="/wiki/E!" title="E!">E!</a>, among others), the film studio <a href="/wiki/Universal_Pictures" title="Universal Pictures">Universal Pictures</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Universal_Parks_%26_Resorts" title="Universal Parks &amp; Resorts">Universal Parks &amp; Resorts</a>. It also has significant holdings in digital distribution, such as <a href="/wiki/ThePlatform" title="ThePlatform">thePlatform</a>, which it acquired in 2006. Since October 2018, it is also the parent company of mass media pan-European company <a href="/wiki/Sky_Group" title="Sky Group">Sky Group</a>, making it the biggest and leading media company with more than 53 million subscribers over five countries across Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast has been criticized for multiple reasons; its customer satisfaction often ranks among the lowest in the cable industry.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JDP-score_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JDP-score-17">[16]</a></sup> In addition, Comcast has violated <a href="/wiki/Net_neutrality" title="Net neutrality">net neutrality</a> practices in the past, and, despite Comcast's commitment to a narrow definition of net neutrality,<sup id="cite_ref-Netflix_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netflix-18">[17]</a></sup> critics advocate a definition which precludes any distinction between Comcast's <a href="/wiki/Private_network" title="Private network">private network</a> services and the rest of the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-FCC-VOIP_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCC-VOIP-19">[18]</a></sup> Critics also point out a lack of competition in the vast majority of Comcast's service area; there is limited competition among cable providers.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> Furthermore, given Comcast's negotiating power as a large ISP, some suspect that Comcast could leverage paid <a href="/wiki/Peering_agreements" class="mw-redirect" title="Peering agreements">peering agreements</a> to unfairly influence end-user connection speeds. Its ownership of both content production (in NBCUniversal) and content distribution (as an ISP) has raised antitrust concerns. These issues, in addition to others, led to Comcast being dubbed "The Worst Company in America" by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Consumerist" class="mw-redirect" title="The Consumerist">The Consumerist</a></i> in 2010 and 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Leadership" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Comcast is sometimes described as a <a href="/wiki/Family_business" title="Family business">family business</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vision_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vision-23">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_L._Roberts" title="Brian L. Roberts">Brian L. Roberts</a>, chairman, president, and CEO of Comcast, is the son of founder <a href="/wiki/Ralph_J._Roberts" title="Ralph J. Roberts">Ralph J. Roberts</a>. Roberts owns or controls about 1% of all Comcast shares but all of the Class B supervoting shares, which gives him an "undilutable 33% voting power over the company".<sup id="cite_ref-note_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-note-24">[23]</a></sup> Legal expert <a href="/wiki/Susan_P._Crawford" title="Susan P. Crawford">Susan P. Crawford</a> has said this gives him "effective control over [Comcast's] every step".<sup id="cite_ref-Crawford_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford-25">[24]</a></sup> In 2010, he was one of the highest paid executives in the United States, with total compensation of about $31 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Crawford_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford-25">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_offices">Corporate offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Corporate offices" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Comcast is headquartered in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, and also has corporate offices in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">Manchester, New Hampshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> On January 3, 2005, Comcast announced that it would become the anchor tenant in the new <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Center_(Philadelphia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Comcast Center (Philadelphia)">Comcast Center</a> in downtown Philadelphia. The 975 ft (297 m) skyscraper is the second tallest building in Pennsylvania. Comcast has since finished construction on a second 1,121 ft (342 m) skyscraper, the tallest building in Pennsylvania, directly adjacent to the original Comcast headquarters in the fall of 2018, known as the <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Technology_Center" title="Comcast Technology Center">Comcast Technology Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> As of 2019 the company has a total of 184,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_relations">Employee relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Employee relations" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company is often criticized by both the media and its own staff for its less upstanding policies regarding employee relations. A 2012 Reddit post written by an anonymous Comcast call center employee eager to share their negative experiences with the public received attention from publications including <i><a href="/wiki/HuffPost" title="HuffPost">The Huffington Post</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> A 2014 investigative series published by <i>The Verge</i> involved interviews with 150 of Comcast's employees. It sought to examine why the company has become so widely criticized by its customers, the media and even members of its own staff. The series claimed part of the problem is internal and that Comcast's staff endures unreasonable corporate policies. According to the report: "customer service has been replaced by an obsession with sales; technicians are understaffed while tech support is poorly trained, and the company is hobbled by internal fragmentation."<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> A widely read article penned by an anonymous call center employee working for Comcast appeared in November 2014 on <i>Cracked</i>. Titled "Five Nightmares You Live While Working For America's Worst Company", the article also claimed that Comcast is obsessed with sales, doesn't train its employees properly and concluded that "the system makes good customer service impossible."<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast has also earned a reputation for being anti-union. According to one of the company's training manuals, "Comcast does not feel union representation is in the best interest of its employees, customers, or shareholders".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> A dispute in 2004 with <a href="/wiki/Communication_Workers_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Communication Workers of America">CWA</a>, a labor union that represented many employees at Comcast's offices in Beaverton, Oregon, led to allegations of management intimidating workers, requiring them to attend anti-union meetings and unwarranted disciplinary action for union members.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> In 2011, Comcast received criticism from <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">Writers Guild of America</a> for its policies in regards to unions.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup></p><p>Despite these criticisms, Comcast has appeared on multiple "top places to work" lists. In 2009, it was included on <i>CableFAX</i> magazine's "Top 10 Places to Work in Cable", which cited its "scale, savvy and vision".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> Similarly, the <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Business_Journal" title="Philadelphia Business Journal">Philadelphia Business Journal</a></i> awarded Comcast the silver medal among extra-large companies in Philadelphia, with the gold medal going to partner organization, Comcast-Spectacor.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> found Comcast to be that city's top place to work in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> Employee diversity is also an attribute upon which Comcast receives strong marks. In 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Enterprise" title="Black Enterprise">Black Enterprise</a></i> magazine rated Comcast among the top 15 companies for workforce diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Comcast was also named a "Top 2014 Workplace" by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> in their annual feature.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a> has given Comcast a 100 on the Corporate Equality Index<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> and one of the best places for LGBT people to work<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_performance">Financial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Financial performance" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The book value of the company nearly doubled from $8.19 a share in 1999 to $15 a share in 2009. Revenues grew sixfold from 1999's $6 billion to almost $36 billion in 2009. Net profit margin rose from 4.2% in 1999 to 8.4% in 2009, with operating margins improving 31% and return on equity doubling to 6.7% in the same time span. Between 1999 and 2009, return on capital nearly tripled to 7%.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-43">[42]</a></sup> Comcast reported first quarter 2012 profit increases of 30% due to increase in high-speed internet customers.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> In February 2014, Comcast generated 1.1 billion in revenue during the first quarter due to the <a href="/wiki/Sochi_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Sochi Olympics">Sochi Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> As of 2018, Comcast is ranked No. 33 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p><p>For the fiscal year 2017, Comcast reported earnings of US$22.7 billion, with an annual revenue of US$84.5 billion, an increase of 5.5% over the previous fiscal cycle. Comcast's shares traded at over $37 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$163.7 billion in October 2018.
</p>

</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Lobbying_and_electoral_fundraising">Lobbying and electoral fundraising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Lobbying and electoral fundraising" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>With $18.8 million spent in 2013, Comcast has the seventh largest <a href="/wiki/Lobbying_in_the_United_States" title="Lobbying in the United States">lobbying</a> budget of any individual company or organization in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-TopSpenders_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopSpenders-61">[60]</a></sup> Comcast employs multiple former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congressmen</a> as lobbyists.<sup id="cite_ref-Web_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Web-62">[61]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Cable_%26_Telecommunications_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="National Cable &amp; Telecommunications Association">National Cable &amp; Telecommunications Association</a>, which has multiple Comcast executives on its board, also represents Comcast and other cable companies as the fifth largest lobbying organization in the United States, spending $19.8 million in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-TopSpenders_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopSpenders-61">[60]</a></sup> Comcast was among the top backers of <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s presidential runs, with Comcast vice president <a href="/wiki/David_L._Cohen" title="David L. Cohen">David Cohen</a> raising over $2.2 million from 2007 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Cohen has been described by many sources as influential in the U.S. government,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> though he is no longer a registered lobbyist, as the time he spends lobbying falls short of the 20% which <a href="/wiki/Lobbying_Disclosure_Act_of_1995" title="Lobbying Disclosure Act of 1995">requires official registration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> Comcast's <a href="/wiki/Political_action_committee" title="Political action committee">PAC</a>, the Comcast Corporation and NBCUniversal Political Action Committee, is among the largest PACs in the U.S., raising about $3.7 million from 2011 to 2012 for the campaigns of various candidates for office in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Federal_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Federal Government">United States Federal Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> Comcast is also a major backer of the National Cable and Telecommunications Association Political Action Committee, which raised $2.6 million from 2011 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Comcast spent the most money of any organization in support of the <a href="/wiki/Stop_Online_Piracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Stop Online Piracy">Stop Online Piracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protect_IP" class="mw-redirect" title="Protect IP">PROTECT IP</a> bills, spending roughly $5 million to lobby for their passage.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast also backs lobbying and PACs on a regional level, backing organizations such as the Tennessee Cable Telecommunications Association<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> and the Broadband Communications Association of Washington PAC.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> Comcast and other cable companies have lobbied state governments to pass legislation restricting or banning individual cities from offering public broadband service.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Municipal_broadband" title="Municipal broadband">Municipal broadband</a> restrictions of varying scope have been passed in a total of 20 U.S. States.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Philanthropy" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Comcast offers low cost internet and cable service to schools, subsidized by general broadband consumers through the U.S. government's <a href="/wiki/E-Rate" title="E-Rate">E-Rate</a> program.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Critics have noted that many of the strongest supporters of Comcast's business deals have received substantial funding from the Comcast Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-Web_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Web-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: History" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Cable_Systems">American Cable Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: American Cable Systems" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1963, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_J._Roberts" title="Ralph J. Roberts">Ralph J. Roberts</a> in conjunction with his two business partners, Daniel Aaron<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Julian_A._Brodsky" title="Julian A. Brodsky">Julian A. Brodsky</a>, purchased <b>American Cable Systems</b><sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup> as a <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">corporate spin-off</a> from its parent, <a href="/wiki/Jerrold_Electronics" title="Jerrold Electronics">Jerrold Electronics</a>, for U.S. $500,000. At the time, American Cable was a small cable operator in <a href="/wiki/Tupelo,_Mississippi" title="Tupelo, Mississippi">Tupelo, Mississippi</a>, with five channels and 12,000 customers.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> In 1965, American Cable Systems purchased Storecast Corporation of America, a product placement supermarket specialist marketing firm.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> In 1968, American Cable Systems purchased its first franchise of Muzak, a brand of background music played in retail stores. Storecast was a client of Muzak.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-81">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Comcast">Comcast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Comcast" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_logo_1963.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Comcast_logo_1963.svg/220px-Comcast_logo_1963.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="28" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="74"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 28px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Comcast_logo_1963.svg/220px-Comcast_logo_1963.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="28" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Comcast_logo_1963.svg/330px-Comcast_logo_1963.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Comcast_logo_1963.svg/440px-Comcast_logo_1963.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_logo_1963.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comcast logo from 1969 to 1999 before it was replaced with the crescent logo</div></div></div>
<p>The company was re-incorporated in Pennsylvania in 1969, under the new name <b>Comcast Corporation</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup> Comcast's <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> occurred on June 29, 1972, with a <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> of U.S. $3,010,000.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> In 1977, <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> was first launched on a Comcast system with 20,000 customers in western Pennsylvania with a five-night free preview getting a 15% sign up rate.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> In 1986, Comcast bought 26% of <a href="/wiki/Group_W_Cable" class="mw-redirect" title="Group W Cable">Group W Cable</a>, a broadcast company, doubling its number of subscribers to 1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Feb-2004-425_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Feb-2004-425-84">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Also that year, Comcast made a founding investment of $380 million in <a href="/wiki/QVC" title="QVC">QVC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup> In 1988, Comcast was able to buy a 50% share of SCI Holdings in a joint deal with <a href="/wiki/Tele-Communications_Inc." title="Tele-Communications Inc.">Tele-Communications Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> Comcast also acquired American Cellular Network Corporation in 1988 for $230 million, marking the first time it became a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_operator" title="Mobile phone operator">mobile phone operator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Increasing_market_share_.281990.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Increasing_market_share_(1990–2000)">Increasing market share (1990–2000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Increasing market share (1990–2000)" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In February 1990, Ralph Roberts' son, Brian L. Roberts, succeeded his father as president of Comcast.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Two years later, the company's mobile division, Comcast Cellular, purchased a controlling interest in <a href="/wiki/Metromedia" title="Metromedia">Metromedia</a>'s Philadelphia-area cellular telephone interests, Metrophone.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> By 1994, Comcast owned 50% stock in the cable communications company <a href="/wiki/Garden_State_Cable" class="mw-redirect" title="Garden State Cable">Garden State Cable</a>, who by that year were serving approximately 195,000 subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> That same year, Comcast became the third-largest cable operator in the United States, with around 3.5 million subscribers following its purchase of <a href="/wiki/Maclean-Hunter" title="Maclean-Hunter">Maclean-Hunter</a>'s American division for $1.27 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Feb-2004-425_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Feb-2004-425-84">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> Comcast grew to 4.3 million subscribers the following year with the purchase of the cable operation of <a href="/wiki/E._W._Scripps_Company" title="E. W. Scripps Company">E. W. Scripps Company</a> for $1.575 billion in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast offered internet connection for the first time in 1996, with its part in the launch of the <a href="/wiki/@Home_Network" title="@Home Network">@Home Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-@Home_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-@Home-93">[92]</a></sup> Also in 1996, Comcast formed <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Spectacor" title="Comcast Spectacor">Comcast Spectacor</a>, which became owner of the Philadelphia Flyers.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> In 1997, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> invested $1 billion in Comcast, and the company launched its digital TV service.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-81">[80]</a></sup> That same year, in partnership with Disney, Comcast got a 50.1% controlling interest in E! Entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup> By December 31, 1997, it was available in the Philadelphia, Detroit, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_CA" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange County, CA">Orange County, CA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarasota,_FL" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarasota, FL">Sarasota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Union_Township,_Union_County,_New_Jersey" title="Union Township, Union County, New Jersey">Union, NJ</a> areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Comcast's cable acquisitions in 1997 were <a href="/wiki/Jones_Intercable" title="Jones Intercable">Jones Intercable, Inc.</a> with 1 million customers, and a stake in Prime Communications with 430,000 subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup> In February 1998, Comcast sold its U.K. division to <a href="/wiki/NTL_Incorporated" title="NTL Incorporated">NTL</a> for US$600 million, along with the division's $397 million in debt.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> In 1999, Comcast sold Comcast Cellular to <a href="/wiki/SBC_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="SBC Communications">SBC Communications</a> for $400 million, releasing them from $1.27 billion in debt.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Also in 1999, Comcast acquired Greater Philadelphia Cablevision,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> and launched Comcast University as well as Comcast Interactive Capital Group.<sup id="cite_ref-mcn_78-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcn-78">[77]</a></sup></p><p>In November 1999, Comcast purchased <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenfest_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lenfest Communications (page does not exist)">Lenfest Communications, Inc.</a> who were the ninth largest cable television operator at the time and were the largest operator in the Philadelphia area.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-99">[98]</a></sup> This consolidated Comcast's control over all of the Philadelphia region, and earned them approximately 1.3 million additional cable subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-99">[98]</a></sup> The purchase of Lenfest also bought Comcast the remaining 50% stock of the cable operator Garden State Communications — a company whom Comcast had already owned half of in partnership with Lenfest for years.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Comcast quickly replaced the ten-year general manager at Garden State with their own executive, and eventually Garden State ceased operating under its own name and was fully merged to become a part of the Comcast Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Largest_U.S._cable_provider_.282001.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_U.S._cable_provider_(2001–present)">Largest U.S. cable provider (2001–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Largest U.S. cable provider (2001–present)" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg/220px-AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="41" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="278" data-file-height="52"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 41px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg/220px-AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="41" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg/330px-AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg/440px-AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AT%26T_Comcast_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Proposed merger name logo, 2001</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_logo_2006.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Comcast_logo_2006.svg/220px-Comcast_logo_2006.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="57" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="682" data-file-height="177"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 57px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Comcast_logo_2006.svg/220px-Comcast_logo_2006.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="57" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Comcast_logo_2006.svg/330px-Comcast_logo_2006.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Comcast_logo_2006.svg/440px-Comcast_logo_2006.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_logo_2006.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comcast logo introduced on December 12, 1999; used from 2000 to 2012 with minor updates in 2007</div></div></div>
<p>In 2001, Comcast announced it would acquire the assets of the largest cable television operator at the time, <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Broadband" title="AT&amp;T Broadband">AT&amp;T Broadband</a>, for U.S.$44.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-AT&amp;T-Dec-2001-8-K_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AT&amp;T-Dec-2001-8-K-102">[101]</a></sup> The proposed name for the merged company was "AT&amp;T Comcast", but the companies ultimately decided to keep only the Comcast name. In 2002, Comcast acquired all assets of AT&amp;T Broadband, thus making Comcast the largest cable television company in the United States with over 22 million subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-AT&amp;T-Dec-2001-8-K_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AT&amp;T-Dec-2001-8-K-102">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AT&amp;T-Nov-2002-8-K_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AT&amp;T-Nov-2002-8-K-103">[102]</a></sup> This spurred the start of Comcast Advertising Sales (using AT&amp;T's groundwork) which would later be renamed <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Spotlight" class="mw-redirect" title="Comcast Spotlight">Comcast Spotlight</a> and now effectv, A Comcast Company. As part of this acquisition, Comcast also acquired the National Digital Television Center in Centennial, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> as a wholly owned subsidiary, now known as the <i>Comcast Media Center</i>. In 2003, Comcast became one of the original investors in <a href="/wiki/Golf_Channel" title="Golf Channel">The Golf Channel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> After Excite@Home went bankrupt in October 2001, Comcast took over providing internet directly to consumers in January 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-@HomeMerge_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-@HomeMerge-105">[104]</a></sup></p><p>On February 11, 2004, Comcast announced a $54 billion bid for <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a>, including taking on $12 billion of Disney's debt.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> The deal would have made Comcast the largest <a href="/wiki/Media_conglomerate" title="Media conglomerate">media conglomerate</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Corp-Feb-2004-8-K_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Corp-Feb-2004-8-K-107">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> However, after rejection by Disney and uncertain response from investors, the bid was abandoned in April.<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Corp-Apr-2004-8-K_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Corp-Apr-2004-8-K-109">[108]</a></sup> In 2004, Comcast sold its QVC shares to <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Media" title="Liberty Media">Liberty Media</a> for $7.9 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup></p><p>On April 8, 2005, a partnership led by Comcast and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Pictures Entertainment">Sony Pictures Entertainment</a> finalized a deal to acquire <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">MGM</a> and its affiliate studio, <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">United Artists</a>, and created an additional outlet to carry MGM/UA's material for cable and Internet distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-Sony-Sep-2004-6-K_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sony-Sep-2004-6-K-111">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sony-Apr-2005-6-K_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sony-Apr-2005-6-K-112">[111]</a></sup> On October 31, 2005, Comcast officially announced that it had acquired <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Susquehanna Communications">Susquehanna Communications</a>, a <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Pennsylvania" title="South Central Pennsylvania">South Central Pennsylvania</a>-based cable television and broadband services provider and unit of the former <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_Pfaltzgraff" title="Susquehanna Pfaltzgraff">Susquehanna Pfaltzgraff</a> company, for $775 million cash.<sup id="cite_ref-Susquehanna-Media-Nov-2005-8-K_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Susquehanna-Media-Nov-2005-8-K-113">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Feb-2006-10-K_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Feb-2006-10-K-114">[113]</a></sup> Comcast previously owned approximately 30% of Susquehanna Communications through its affiliate company, <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Lenfest" title="Gerry Lenfest">Lenfest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Susquehanna-Media-Nov-2005-8-K_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Susquehanna-Media-Nov-2005-8-K-113">[112]</a></sup> In December 2005, Comcast announced the creation of <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Interactive_Media" title="Comcast Interactive Media">Comcast Interactive Media</a>, a new division focused on online media.
</p><p>In July 2006, Comcast purchased the Seattle-based software company thePlatform.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> This represented an entry into a new line of business – selling software to allow companies to manage their Internet (and IP-based) media publishing efforts.
</p><p>On April 3, 2007, Comcast announced it would acquire the cable systems owned and operated by Patriot Media, a privately held company owned by cable veteran Steven J. Simmons, <a href="/wiki/Spectrum_Equity_Investors" class="mw-redirect" title="Spectrum Equity Investors">Spectrum Equity Investors</a> and Spire Capital, that served approximately 81,000 video subscribers for $483 million.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast announced in May 2007<sup id="cite_ref-Martens_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens-117">[116]</a></sup> and launched in September 2008 a dashboard called SmartZone that allowed users to perform mobile functions online.<sup id="cite_ref-Kukec_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kukec-118">[117]</a></sup> There was also Cloudmark <a href="/wiki/E-mail_spam" class="mw-redirect" title="E-mail spam">spam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phishing" title="Phishing">phishing</a> protection and <a href="/wiki/Trend_Micro" title="Trend Micro">Trend Micro</a> <a href="/wiki/Antivirus_software" title="Antivirus software">antivirus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Martens_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens-117">[116]</a></sup> The address book is Comcast <a href="/wiki/Plaxo" title="Plaxo">Plaxo</a> software.<sup id="cite_ref-Martens_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens-117">[116]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2008 Comcast purchased Plaxo for a reported $150 million to $170 million.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast won the <i>Consumerist</i> Worst Company In America ("Golden Poo") award in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> A gold trophy in the shape of a pile of <a href="/wiki/Human_feces" title="Human feces">human feces</a> was delivered to Comcast Corporate Headquarters to commemorate the unmatched level of enmity flowing from their customer base to their business. Comcast responded immediately by publicly acknowledging the dubious award and citing ongoing efforts to improve its customer service.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> One effort to change this is a new app called Tech ETA that allows customers to see exactly when a technician is coming.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Adelphia_purchase">Adelphia purchase</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Adelphia purchase" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In April 2005, Comcast and Time Warner Cable announced plans to buy the assets of bankrupted <a href="/wiki/Adelphia_Communications_Corporation" title="Adelphia Communications Corporation">Adelphia Cable</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Adelphia_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adelphia-123">[122]</a></sup> The two companies paid a total of $17.6 billion in the deal that was finalized in the second quarter of 2006—after the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Federal_Communications_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Federal Communications Commission">U.S. Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC) completed a seven-month investigation without raising an objection.<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Apr-2005-8-K_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Apr-2005-8-K-124">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable" title="Time Warner Cable">Time Warner Cable</a> became the second-largest cable provider in the U.S., ranking behind Comcast. As part of the deal, Time Warner and Comcast traded existing subscribers in order to consolidate them into larger geographic clusters.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2006, Comcast and Time Warner dissolved a 50/50 partnership that controlled the systems in the <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Southwest Texas, <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Metropolitan Area">Kansas City</a> markets under the Time Warner brand. After the dissolution, Comcast obtained the Houston system, and Time Warner retained the others.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> On January 1, 2007, Comcast officially took control of the Houston system but continued to operate under the Time Warner Cable brand until June 19, 2007.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: NBCUniversal" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_NBC_Universal_by_Comcast" title="Acquisition of NBC Universal by Comcast">Acquisition of NBC Universal by Comcast</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NBC_Universal.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/NBC_Universal.svg/220px-NBC_Universal.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="85" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="522" data-file-height="202"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 85px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/NBC_Universal.svg/220px-NBC_Universal.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="85" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/NBC_Universal.svg/330px-NBC_Universal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/NBC_Universal.svg/440px-NBC_Universal.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NBC_Universal.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a> logo from 2004 to 2011</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NBCUniversal_Logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NBCUniversal_Logo.svg/220px-NBCUniversal_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="25" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1348" data-file-height="153"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 25px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NBCUniversal_Logo.svg/220px-NBCUniversal_Logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="25" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NBCUniversal_Logo.svg/330px-NBCUniversal_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NBCUniversal_Logo.svg/440px-NBCUniversal_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NBCUniversal_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NBCUniversal logo from 2011 to present</div></div></div>
<p>Media outlets began reporting in late September 2009 that Comcast was in talks to buy <a href="/wiki/NBC_Universal" class="mw-redirect" title="NBC Universal">NBC Universal</a>. Comcast denied the rumors at first, while NBC would not comment on them.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> However, CNBC itself reported on October 1 that <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> was considering spinning NBC Universal off into a separate company that would merge the NBC television network and its cable properties such as USA Network, Syfy and MSNBC, as well as Universal Studios, with Comcast's content assets. GE would maintain 49% control of the new company, while Comcast owned 51%.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vivendi" title="Vivendi">Vivendi</a>, which owns 20%, would have to sell its stake to GE. It was reported that under the current deal with GE that it would happen in November or December.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> It was also reported that <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a> would be interested in placing a bid, until CEO <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_L._Bewkes" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeffrey L. Bewkes">Jeffrey L. Bewkes</a> directly denied interest,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> leaving Comcast the sole bidder. On November 1, 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported Comcast had moved closer to a deal to purchase NBC Universal and that a formal announcement could be made sometime the following week.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p><p>Following a tentative agreement on December 1,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> the parties announced that Comcast would buy a controlling 51% stake in NBCUniversal for $6.5 billion in cash and $7.3 billion in programming on December 3.<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Dec-2009-8-K_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Dec-2009-8-K-136">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comcastnbc_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comcastnbc-137">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> GE would take over the remaining 49% stake in NBC Universal, using $5.8 billion to buy out Vivendi's 20% minority stake in NBC Universal.<sup id="cite_ref-comcastnbc_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comcastnbc-137">[136]</a></sup> On January 18, 2011, the FCC approved the deal by a vote of 4 to 1.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> The sale was completed on January 28, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> In late December 2012, Comcast decided to shed the crescent logo and added the NBC peacock symbol to their new logo.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> On February 12, 2013, Comcast announced an intention to acquire the remaining 49% of General Electric's interest in NBCUniversal,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> which Comcast completed on March 19, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Comcast-Mar-2013-8-K_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comcast-Mar-2013-8-K-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CMCSA-GE_Final_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMCSA-GE_Final-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Failed_purchase_of_Time_Warner_Cable">Failed purchase of Time Warner Cable</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Failed purchase of Time Warner Cable" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Attempted_purchase_of_Time_Warner_Cable_by_Comcast" title="Attempted purchase of Time Warner Cable by Comcast">Attempted purchase of Time Warner Cable by Comcast</a></div>
<p>On February 12, 2014, the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> reported that Comcast sought to acquire Time Warner Cable in a deal valued at $45.2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> On February 13, it was reported that Time Warner Cable agreed to the acquisition.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> This was to add several metropolitan areas to the Comcast portfolio, such as New York City, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dallas-Fort_Worth" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas-Fort Worth">Dallas-Fort Worth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlotte">Charlotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, and San Antonio.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> Time Warner Cable and Comcast aimed to merge into one company by the end of 2014 and both have praised the deal, emphasizing the increased capabilities of a combined telecommunications network, and to "create operating efficiencies and economies of scale".<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, critics expressed concern that the deal would give Comcast greater negotiating power in a number of areas, including <a href="/wiki/Rebroadcast_fee" class="mw-redirect" title="Rebroadcast fee">rebroadcast fees</a> with television channels,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Peering_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Peering agreement">peering agreements</a> with ISPs.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup></p><p>Critics noted in 2013 that <a href="/wiki/Tom_Wheeler_(FCC)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Wheeler (FCC)">Tom Wheeler</a>, the head of the FCC, which has to approve the deal, is the former head of both the largest cable lobbying organization, the National Cable &amp; Telecommunications Association, and as largest wireless lobby, <a href="/wiki/CTIA_%E2%80%93_The_Wireless_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="CTIA – The Wireless Association">CTIA – The Wireless Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/Politico" title="Politico">Politico</a></i>, Comcast "donated to almost every member of Congress who has a hand in regulating it".<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_the_Judiciary" title="United States Senate Committee on the Judiciary">US Senate Judiciary Committee</a> held a hearing on the deal on April 9, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/House_Judiciary_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="House Judiciary Committee">House Judiciary Committee</a> planned its own hearing.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> On March 6, 2014, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice_Antitrust_Division" title="United States Department of Justice Antitrust Division">United States Department of Justice Antitrust Division</a> confirmed it was investigating the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> In March 2014, the division's chairman, William Baer, recused himself because he was involved in the prior Comcast NBCUniversal acquisition.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> Several states' attorneys general have announced support for the federal investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> On April 24, 2015, Jonathan Sallet, general counsel of the F.C.C., said that he was going to recommend a hearing before an administrative law judge, equivalent to a collapse of the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-161">[160]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2015, Comcast announced to speed up Internet for low-income customers from 5 megabits per second (mbps) to 10 Mbit/s, provide free wireless routers, and will pilot an initiative to increase Internet access for low-income senior citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-boston_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boston-162">[161]</a></sup> In September of that year Comcast also launched Watchable, a <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> competitor.<sup id="cite_ref-watchablevar_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watchablevar-163">[162]</a></sup> The move was seen by <a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a> as an attempt to appeal to the <a href="/wiki/Cord_cutting" class="mw-redirect" title="Cord cutting">cord cutting</a> market.<sup id="cite_ref-watchablevar_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watchablevar-163">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="DreamWorks_Animation">DreamWorks Animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: DreamWorks Animation" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks Animation</a></div>
<p>In April 2016, Comcast confirmed that its NBCUniversal division would acquire <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks Animation</a> for $3.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> The deal closed on August 22, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> Universal Pictures took over distribution of DreamWorks Animation films beginning in 2019 with <i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Train_Your_Dragon:_The_Hidden_World" title="How to Train Your Dragon: The Hidden World">How to Train Your Dragon: The Hidden World</a></i> after DreamWorks Animation's deal with <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Studios" title="20th Century Studios">20th Century Fox</a> expired.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Cellular_service">Cellular service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cellular service" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In September 2016, Comcast confirmed that it had reached a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon Wireless</a> to launch a <a href="/wiki/Cellular_network" title="Cellular network">cellular network</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Virtual_Network_Operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile Virtual Network Operator">MVNO</a>. The new service, described as being a "Wi-Fi and MVNO-integrated product", and was expected to launch in mid-2017.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> The partnership and the addition of wireless would allow Comcast to offer a <a href="/wiki/Quadruple_play" title="Quadruple play">quadruple play</a> of services.<sup id="cite_ref-verge-comcastmvno_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-comcastmvno-168">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> Including Comcast's Home Security offering, customers now have the option of a Quintuple Play.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> The service was officially announced on April 6, 2017, as Xfinity Mobile.<sup id="cite_ref-phillycom-xfinitymobile_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phillycom-xfinitymobile-171">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Attempted_acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox">Attempted acquisition of 21st Century Fox</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Attempted acquisition of 21st Century Fox" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney" title="Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney">Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney</a></div>
<p>On November 16, 2017, it is reported that Comcast attempted to purchase <a href="/wiki/21st_Century_Fox" title="21st Century Fox">21st Century Fox</a>, following the news 10 days earlier that The Walt Disney Company negotiated with Fox to acquire the same assets. Like Disney, the deal included the 20th Century Fox film and television studios, cable entertainment and broadcast satellite networks including <a href="/wiki/FX_(TV_channel)" title="FX (TV channel)">FX Networks</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Partners" title="National Geographic Partners">National Geographic Partners</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Networks" title="Fox Sports Networks">Fox Sports Networks</a>, and international channels such as <a href="/wiki/Star_India" title="Star India">Star India</a>. It would not include the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox Broadcasting Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Television_Stations" title="Fox Television Stations">Fox Television Stations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(United_States)" title="Fox Sports (United States)">Fox Sports</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> units, all which will be spun-off into a new independent company,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> which is later known as the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Corporation" title="Fox Corporation">Fox Corporation</a>.
</p><p>However, on December 11, 2017, Comcast officially dropped the bid, saying that "We never got the level of engagement needed to make a definitive offer.”<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> On December 14, Disney officially confirmed its acquisition of 21st Century Fox for $52.4 billion in stock, pending review from the United States Department of Justice Antitrust Division.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup></p><p>On February 5, 2018, a new report by CNBC claims that despite the Disney/Fox deal, Comcast was considering topping Disney's $52.4 billion offer once the <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>–<a href="/wiki/WarnerMedia" title="WarnerMedia">Time Warner</a> merger goes through, after the Department of Justice Antitrust Division sued to block the merger on November 20, 2017.
</p><p>On May 7, 2018, Comcast announced a potential bid against Disney's effort to acquire Fox after it spoke to investment banks about making a $60 billion cash offer, pending on approval of the AT&amp;T-Time Warner merger.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> On May 15, several Fox investors expressed interests in inking a deal with Comcast due to their all-cash offer as opposed to Disney's $52.4 billion stock offer.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> On June 13, Comcast officially announced a $65 billion counter-offer to acquire the 21st Century Fox's assets that Disney offered to purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup></p><p>However, on June 20, 2018, Disney and Fox announced that they had amended their previous merger agreement, upping Disney's offer to $71.3 billion (a 10% premium over Comcast's $65 billion offer), while also offering shareholders the option of receiving cash instead of stock.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-178">[177]</a></sup> On June 27, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> gave antitrust approval to Disney under the condition of selling Fox's 22 regional sports channels, to which the company has agreed.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> On the next day, Disney and Fox shareholders scheduled July 27, 2018 as the day to vote on Fox's properties being sold to Disney, giving Comcast enough time to make a higher counter-offer for the Fox assets.<sup id="cite_ref-Vote-07-27-Variety_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vote-07-27-Variety-180">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vote-07-27-LATimes_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vote-07-27-LATimes-181">[180]</a></sup></p><p>However, on July 12, 2018, the Department of Justice filed a notice of appeal with the D.C. Circuit to reverse the District Court's approval for AT&amp;T acquisition of Time Warner (now renamed WarnerMedia). Although analysts say that the chances of the DOJ win are small, they say it is the "final nail in the coffin for Comcast's Fox chase. This is a clear gift to Disney."<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> On the next day, CEO of AT&amp;T <a href="/wiki/Randall_Stephenson" class="mw-redirect" title="Randall Stephenson">Randall Stephenson</a> gave an interview with CNBC, about Comcast's bid for Fox: "It probably can't help it. You're in a situation where two entities are bidding for an asset, and this kind of action can obviously influence the outcome of those actions."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup></p><p>On July 16, 2018, CNBC reported that Comcast was unlikely to continue its bidding war to acquire Fox from Disney in favor of <a href="/wiki/Sky_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky (company)">Sky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> On July 19, 2018, Comcast officially announced that it was dropping its bid on the Fox assets in order to focus on their bid for Sky. CEO of Comcast, Brian L. Roberts said: “I’d like to congratulate Bob Iger and the team at Disney and commend the Murdoch family and Fox for creating such a desirable and respected company."<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_of_Sky_plc">Acquisition of Sky plc</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Acquisition of Sky plc" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On February 27, 2018, Comcast offered to purchase 61% stake in Sky plc at a value of £12.50 per-share, approximately £22.1 billion. 21st Century Fox, which owns 39% stake in Sky, had previously declined a US$60 billion acquisition offer by Comcast in favor of its deal with Disney, due to anti-competition concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> NBCUniversal CEO <a href="/wiki/Steve_Burke_(businessman)" title="Steve Burke (businessman)">Steve Burke</a> stated that purchasing Sky would roughly double its presence in English-speaking markets, and allow for synergies between the respective networks and studios of NBCUniversal and Sky. Fox stated that it "remains committed to its recommended cash offer for Sky", and that Comcast had not yet made a "firm offer".<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup></p><p>On April 12, the <a href="/wiki/Panel_on_Takeovers_and_Mergers" title="Panel on Takeovers and Mergers">Panel on Takeovers and Mergers</a> ruled that Disney had to acquire all of Sky within 28 days of fully acquiring Fox if the latter's acquisition of Sky was not completed by the time the merger was done, or if Comcast's counter-offer wasn't accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> On April 25, 2018, Comcast made its formal counter-bid for Sky plc, offering £12.50 per-share; Sky subsequently withdrew its recommendation of the Fox bid.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> On June 5, 2018, <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Digital,_Culture,_Media_and_Sport" title="Secretary of State for Digital, Culture, Media and Sport">Culture Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hancock" title="Matt Hancock">Matt Hancock</a> cleared both 21st Century Fox and Comcast's respective offers to acquire Sky plc. Fox's offer is contingent on the divestiture of Sky News.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup></p><p>On June 15, 2018, the European Commission gave antitrust clearance to Comcast's offer to purchase Sky, citing that in terms of their current assets in Europe, there would be limited impact on competition. Comcast included a 10-year commitment to the operations and funding of Sky News similar to that of Disney's offer.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> On June 19, 2018, Disney formally agreed to acquire Sky News as part of Fox's proposed bid, with a 15-year commitment to increase its annual funding from £90 million to £100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup></p><p>On July 11, 2018, 21st Century Fox raised its bid to purchase Sky plc assets to $32.5 billion, and $18.57 a share. In response, Comcast increased its bid to $34 billion, and $19.5 a share. At the same time, Fox was given clearance by the British government to purchase Sky.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> On July 18, 2018, <i>Bloomberg</i> reported that the Sky board scheduled July 27, 2018 as the day shareholders vote on selling Sky properties.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup></p><p>On September 22, 2018, Comcast outbid 21st Century Fox, by raising its bid for Sky plc to $40 billion, or $22.57 a share.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> On September 25, 2018, Comcast bought a 30% stake of Sky plc.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> The next day on September 26, 2018, Fox with the consent of its acquirer sold its 39% stake to Comcast in exchange for $15 billion in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> In October 2018 Comcast later acquired the rest of the shares of Sky with the company being dislisted in November.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> The merger closed on November 7 with the company being dislisted after becoming a wholly owned subsidiary and division of Comcast.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Xumo_acquisition">Xumo acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Xumo acquisition" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On February 25, 2020, Comcast announced it would purchase <a href="/wiki/Xumo" title="Xumo">Xumo</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a>/Viant joint venture for an undisclosed sum. The acquisition of the service—which will continue to operate as an independent business, albeit within Comcast's cable television division—stems mainly from Xumo’s partnerships with <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">smart TV</a> manufacturers (including <a href="/wiki/LG_Electronics" title="LG Electronics">LG</a>, Panasonic and <a href="/wiki/Vizio" title="Vizio">Vizio</a>), which would allow Comcast to use Xumo’s placement to market or showcase Xfinity and other Comcast services as well as use its technology to develop additional streaming platforms. The company plans to add content from the NBCUniversal programming library and the company's various television networks as well as use it to upsell its free/subscription hybrid service <a href="/wiki/Peacock_(streaming_service)" title="Peacock (streaming service)">Peacock</a>, akin to <a href="/wiki/ViacomCBS" title="ViacomCBS">ViacomCBS</a>'s utilization of <a href="/wiki/Pluto_TV" title="Pluto TV">Pluto TV</a> to offer content from its cable networks following the former <a href="/wiki/Viacom_(2005%E2%80%932019)" title="Viacom (2005–2019)">Viacom</a>'s purchase of the rival streamer in the Spring of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup></p>
