</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisions_and_subsidiaries">Divisions and subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Divisions and subsidiaries" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_Comcast" title="List of assets owned by Comcast">List of assets owned by Comcast</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Comcast_Cable_.28Xfinity.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Comcast_Cable_(Xfinity)">Comcast Cable (Xfinity)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Comcast Cable (Xfinity)" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Xfinity" title="Xfinity">Xfinity</a></div>
<p>Comcast Cable is the cable television division of Comcast Corporation, providing cable television, broadband internet, and landline telephone under the Xfinity brand. Comcast Cable also provides connections to small to medium-sized business through its <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Business" title="Comcast Business">Comcast Business</a> brand, and Fortune 1000 companies through its Comcast Enterprise brand.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="NBCUniversal_2">NBCUniversal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: NBCUniversal" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a></div>
<p>Comcast delivers third-party television programming content to its own customers, and also produces its own first-party content both for subscribers and customers of other competing television services. Fully or partially owned Comcast programming includes Comcast Newsmakers, <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Network" title="Comcast Network">Comcast Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comcast_SportsNet" class="mw-redirect" title="Comcast SportsNet">Comcast SportsNet</a>, <a href="/wiki/SportsNet_New_York" title="SportsNet New York">SportsNet New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/MLB_Network" title="MLB Network">MLB Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Sports_Southeast/Charter_Sports_Southeast" class="mw-redirect" title="Comcast Sports Southeast/Charter Sports Southeast">Comcast Sports Southeast/Charter Sports Southeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="NBC Sports Network">NBC Sports Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Golf_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="The Golf Channel">The Golf Channel</a>, Syfy, and USA Network. On May 19, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Disney" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney">Disney</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> announced an agreement to allow Comcast Corporation to carry the channels <a href="/wiki/ESPNU" title="ESPNU">ESPNU</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN3" title="ESPN3">ESPN3</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-espnmediazone.com_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnmediazone.com-210">[209]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast's content networks and assets also include E!, <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_(TV_channel)" title="Oxygen (TV channel)">Oxygen</a>, Golf Channel, NBCSN, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Kids" title="Universal Kids">Universal Kids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bravo_(U.S._TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bravo (U.S. TV network)">Bravo</a>, and the regional <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports_Regional_Networks" title="NBC Sports Regional Networks">NBC Sports Networks</a>. When Comcast took majority ownership in NBCUniversal, a significant number of cable networks were added to this list. Comcast's NHL deal obligated them to create a U.S. version of <a href="/wiki/NHL_Network_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="NHL Network (United States)">NHL Network</a>, launched in October 2007.
</p><p>Comcast has also operated local channels in some markets, such as Comcast Television in the Detroit region, Comcast Network in the Philadelphia and Mid-Atlantic regions (formerly CN8), and Comcast Entertainment Television in Denver and parts of Utah. They primarily carried local programs and sports (including, in some cases, serving as the designated overflow channel for local <a href="/wiki/Regional_sports_network" title="Regional sports network">regional sports networks</a>).
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="DreamWorks_Animation_2">DreamWorks Animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: DreamWorks Animation" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On August 22, 2016, NBCUniversal bought DreamWorks Animation, along with its major IPs including <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_(franchise)" title="Shrek (franchise)">Shrek</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Train_Your_Dragon_(franchise)" class="mw-redirect" title="How to Train Your Dragon (franchise)">How to Train Your Dragon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kung_Fu_Panda_(franchise)" title="Kung Fu Panda (franchise)">Kung Fu Panda</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Madagascar_(franchise)" title="Madagascar (franchise)">Madagascar</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR-Dreamworks-Buyout_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR-Dreamworks-Buyout-211">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN-Dreamworks-Buyout_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-Dreamworks-Buyout-212">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AP-Dreamworks-Buyout_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP-Dreamworks-Buyout-213">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WSJ-Dreamworks-Buyout_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-Dreamworks-Buyout-214">[213]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sky_Group">Sky Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sky Group" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sky_Group" title="Sky Group">Sky Group</a></div>
<p>Through Sky, Comcast offers any first-party and third-party television programming which using the <a href="/wiki/Satellite_television" title="Satellite television">satellite distribution</a> system  to its customers and subscribers across several Europe countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. It is Europe's largest media company and <a href="/wiki/Pay_television" title="Pay television">pay-TV</a> broadcaster by revenue (as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>),<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> with 23 million subscribers and more than 31,000 employees as of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Key_facts_and_figures_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Key_facts_and_figures-216">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-News_Corp._slows_BSkyB_bid_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-News_Corp._slows_BSkyB_bid-217">[216]</a></sup></p><p>Until November 2018, Sky was owned by 21st Century Fox through a 39.14% controlling stake;<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> on 9 December 2016, following a previous attempt under <a href="/wiki/News_Corporation_(1980%E2%80%932013)" title="News Corporation (1980–2013)">News Corporation</a> that was affected by the <a href="/wiki/News_International_phone_hacking_scandal" title="News International phone hacking scandal">News International phone hacking scandal</a>, 21st Century Fox announced that it had agreed to buy the remainder of Sky, pending government approval. However, after a bidding war that included Disney (which was, in turn, acquiring most of 21st Century Fox assets), Comcast acquired the entirety of Sky in 2018 for £17.28 per-share.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_sports">Professional sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Professional sports" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Spectacor" title="Comcast Spectacor">Comcast Spectacor</a></div>
<p>In 1996, Comcast bought a controlling stake in Spectacor from the company's founder, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Snider" title="Ed Snider">Ed Snider</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> Comcast Spectacor holdings now include the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Philadelphia Flyers</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> hockey team and their home arena in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>. Over a number of years, Comcast became majority owner of Comcast SportsNet, as well as Golf Channel and NBCSN (formerly the Outdoor Life Network, then Versus). In 2002, Comcast paid the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland</a> $25 million for <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a> to the new basketball arena built on the College Park campus, the <a href="/wiki/Xfinity_Center_(College_Park,_Maryland)" title="Xfinity Center (College Park, Maryland)">Xfinity Center</a>. Before it was renamed for Comcast's cable subsidiary, Xfinity Center was called Comcast Center from its opening in 2002 through July 2014. Comcast became the sponsor of <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>'s second tier series renaming it the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Xfinity_Series" title="NASCAR Xfinity Series">NASCAR Xfinity Series</a> in 2015.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Venture_capital">Venture capital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Venture capital" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Ventures" title="Comcast Ventures">Comcast Ventures</a></div>
<p>Comcast founded its first <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> fund in January 1999, as Comcast Interactive Capital.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup> Around 2011, following the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_NBC_Universal_by_Comcast" title="Acquisition of NBC Universal by Comcast">NBC Universal acquisition</a>, <i>Comcast Interactive Capital</i> was merged with<i> The Peacock Equity Fund</i>, the venture capital subsidiary of NBCUniversal.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup> The combined company, <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Ventures" title="Comcast Ventures">Comcast Ventures</a>, is led by <a href="/wiki/Amy_Banse" title="Amy Banse">Amy Banse</a> as Head of Funds 
<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup>
and backs various companies such as <a href="/wiki/FanDuel" title="FanDuel">FanDuel</a><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vox_Media" title="Vox Media">Vox Media</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup> for example.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_controversy">Criticism and controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Criticism and controversy" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Comcast" title="Criticism of Comcast">Criticism of Comcast</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_service_van.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Comcast_service_van.jpg/220px-Comcast_service_van.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="7038" data-file-height="4006"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 125px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Comcast_service_van.jpg/220px-Comcast_service_van.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="125" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_service_van.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comcast service van, <a href="/wiki/Ypsilanti_Township,_Michigan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ypsilanti Township, Michigan">Ypsilanti Township</a>, Michigan</div></div></div>
<p>In 2004 and 2007, the <a href="/wiki/American_Customer_Satisfaction_Index" title="American Customer Satisfaction Index">American Customer Satisfaction Index</a> (ACSI) survey found that Comcast had the worst customer satisfaction rating of any company or government agency in the country, including the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a>. The ACSI indicates that almost half of all cable customers (regardless of company) have registered complaints, and that cable is the only industry to score below 60 in the ACSI.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> Comcast's Customer Service Rating by the ACSI surveys indicate that the company's customer service has not improved since the surveys began in 2001. Analysis of the surveys states that "Comcast is one of the lowest scoring companies in ACSI. As its customer satisfaction eroded by 7% over the past year, revenue increased by 12%." The ACSI analysis also addresses this contradiction, stating that "Such <a href="/wiki/Pricing_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Pricing power">pricing power</a> usually comes with some level of monopoly protection and most cable companies have little competition at the local level. This also means that a cable company can do well financially even though its customers are not particularly satisfied."<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2014, Comcast was awarded the 2014 "Worst Company in America" award; an annual contest by the consumer affairs blog <i>The Consumerist</i> that runs a series of reader polls to determine the least popular company in America. This was the second time Comcast had been awarded this title, the first being in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast spends millions of dollars annually on <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lobbying_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lobbying-230">[229]</a></sup> Comcast employs the spouses, sons and daughters of mayors, councilmen, commissioners, and other officials to assure its continued preferred market allocations.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost2006_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost2006-232">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-233">[232]</a></sup></p><p>Comcast was given an "F" for its corporate governance practices in 2010, by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Corporate_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Corporate Library (page does not exist)">Corporate Library</a>, an independent shareholder-research organization. According to Corporate Library, Comcast's board of directors ability to oversee and control management was severely compromised (at least in 2010) by the fact that several of the directors either worked for the company or had business ties to it (making them susceptible to management pressure), and a third of the directors were over 70 years of age. According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> nearly two-thirds of the flights of Comcast's $40 million corporate jet purchased for business travel related to the NBCU acquisition, were to CEO Brian Roberts' private homes or to resorts.<sup id="cite_ref-Maremont_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maremont-234">[233]</a></sup></p><p>On August 1, 2016, Washington State Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Bob_Ferguson_(politician)" title="Bob Ferguson (politician)">Bob Ferguson</a> filed a lawsuit against Comcast Corporation in King County Superior Court, alleging the company's own documents reveal a pattern of illegally deceiving their customers to pad their bottom line by tens of millions of dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> The FCC issued a $2.3 million fine to Comcast after finding that the company was charging customers for unordered services and equipment. More than a thousand customers issued complaints about these unprecedented charges to their bill. In addition, numerous customers reported inappropriate name-calling and interrogation by customer service representatives. Comcast's executive vice president, David Cohen, admitted the company needed to improve their customer service.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup></p><p>On August 8, 2016 an official Comcast employee confirmed that Comcast was changing native 1080i channels to the 720p60 format. "Official Employees are from multiple teams within Comcast: Product, Support, Leadership."<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2017, Comcast was ordered by the self-regulatory <a href="/wiki/Advertising_Self-Regulatory_Council" title="Advertising Self-Regulatory Council">National Advertising Review Board</a> to cease using a claim based on <a href="/wiki/Speedtest.net" title="Speedtest.net">Speedtest.net</a> data that it has "America's fastest internet", stating that "Ookla’s data showed only that Xfinity consumers who took advantage of the free tests offered on the Speedtest.net website subscribed to tiers of service with higher download speeds than Verizon FiOS consumers who took advantage of the tests." They were also ordered to stop using a claim that the company offers the "fastest in-home Wi-Fi," which was poorly substantiated.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-fastestnot_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-fastestnot-238">[237]</a></sup></p><p>As of fall 2019, Comcast is the last major cable provider or streamer to neglect to carry the <a href="/wiki/ACC_Network" title="ACC Network">ACC Network</a>, prompting some customers to consider <a href="/wiki/Cord-cutting" title="Cord-cutting">cutting the cord</a> or switching providers.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U-Verse_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U-Verse-240">[239]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes (magazine)">Forbes</a></i> magazine criticized the decision to not carry the college sports network as violating a fundamental principle of marketing: "never give your customers a reason to switch."<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> Governor <a href="/wiki/Roy_Cooper" title="Roy Cooper">Roy Cooper</a> asked Comcast and AT&amp;T to carry the network, after which AT&amp;T did so on their <a href="/wiki/U-Verse" class="mw-redirect" title="U-Verse">U-Verse</a> cable service.<sup id="cite_ref-U-Verse_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U-Verse-240">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references"><li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Before the <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Broadband" title="AT&amp;T Broadband">AT&amp;T</a> merger in 2001, the parent company was <b>Comcast Holdings Corporation</b>. Comcast Holdings Corporation now refers to a subsidiary of Comcast Corporation, not the parent company (see: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://investing.businessweek.com/research/stocks/private/snapshot.asp?privcapId=7675764">Bloomberg profile on Comcast Holdings Corporation</a>). Technically, the current parent company was founded December 7, 2001 as <b>CAB Holdings Corporation</b>, which changed its name to <b>AT&amp;T Comcast Corporation</b> before finally taking on the <b>Comcast Corporation</b> name (see: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://apps.shareholder.com/sec/viewerContent.aspx?companyid=CMCSA&amp;docid=2086089">Nov 2002 8K/A Form</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140325052620/http://apps.shareholder.com/sec/viewerContent.aspx?companyid=CMCSA&amp;docid=2086089">Archived</a> March 25, 2014, at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cmcsa.com/secfiling.cfm?filingID=950103-02-1156">Nov 2002 S-4</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140325044519/http://www.cmcsa.com/secfiling.cfm?filingID=950103-02-1156">Archived</a> March 25, 2014, at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>).</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comcast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: References" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
